## Problem
Let $\Omega$ and $\Gamma$ be circles with centres $M$ and $N$, respectively, such that the radius of $\Omega$ is less than the radius of $\Gamma$. Suppose $\Omega$ and $\Gamma$ intersect at two distinct points $A$ and $B$. Line $MN$ intersects $\Omega$ at $C$ and $\Gamma$ at $D$, so that $C, M, N, D$ lie on $MN$ in that order. Let's compute coordinates.

LetŌĆÖs compute.

A = (x0, y0). We have x0 = (d^2 + r^2 - R^2) / (2d). We also have y0^2 = r^2 - x0^2. We'll keep y0.

P = (p_x, p_y). Then |P C|^2 = (p_x - (-r))^2 + (p_y - 0)^2 = (p_x + r)^2 + p_y^2.
|P A|^2 = (p_x - x0)^2 + (p_y - y0)^2.

Set equal:

(p_x + r)^2 + p_y^2 = (p_x - x0)^2 + (p_y - y0)^2.

Expand:

(p_x^2 + 2p_x r + r^2) + p_y^2 = (p_x^2 - 2p_x x0 + x0^2) + (p_y^2 - 2p_y y0 + y0^2).

Cancel p_x^2 and p_y^2:

2p_x r + r^2 = -2p_x x0 + x0^2 - 2p_y y0 + y0^2.

So bring terms: 2p_x r + r^2 + 2p_x x0 - x0^2 + 2p_y y0 - y0^2 = 0.

But we can use that x0^2 + y0^2 = r^2 => y0^2 = r^2 - x0^2. Then - y0^2 = -r^2 + x0^2. Substitute.

Then 2p_x r + r^2 + 2p_x x0 - x0^2 + 2p_y y0 - (r^2 - x0^2) = 0 => 2p_x r + r^2 + 2p_x x0 - x0^2 + 2p_y y0 - r^2 + x0^2 = 0 => 2p_x r + 2p_x x0 + 2p_y y0 = 0.

So we get:

2p_x (r + x0) + 2p_y y0 = 0 => p_x (r + x0) + p_y y0 = 0.

Thus p_y = - p_x (r + x0) / y0.

That's an expression. Let's compute p_x and r + x0. p_x = (d + R - r)/2.

Now, we can compute P:

p_y = (1 - c d) / (2*1) = (1 - (u - r)*(v + R)) / 2.

So P = (p_x, p_y). That's fine.

Now, compute H:

H = (p_x, h_H) with h_H = 1 - (p_x - u)*(p_x - v) / (p_y - 1). Since p_y - 1 = p_y - 1.

LetŌĆÖs denote P = (p1, p2). Then:

Equation (A): p1 x + p2 y = ((╬▒+╬▓)/2) (p1^2 + p2^2).   (1)

Equation from |O - B|^2 = |O - ╬▒ P|^2: 

(O - B)┬Ę(O - B) = (O - ╬▒ P)┬Ę(O - ╬▒ P) ŌåÆ |O|^2 - 2 O┬ĘB + |B|^2 = |O|^2 - 2╬▒ O┬ĘP + ╬▒^2 |P|^2 ŌåÆ -2 O┬ĘB + 4 = -2╬▒ (p1 x + p2 y) + ╬▒^2 |P|^2.   (2)

But O┬ĘB = 2 y. So:

-4 y + 4 = -2╬▒ (p1 x + p2 y) + ╬▒^2 |P|^2.

Thus:

2╬▒ (p1 x + p2 y) - 4 y = ╬▒^2 |P|^2 - 4.

Divide by 2: ╬▒ (p1 x + p2 y) - 2 y = (╬▒^2 |P|^2)/2 - 2.   (2a)

Now, we also have from (1) that p1 x + p2 y = K, where K = ((╬▒+╬▓)/2) |P|^2. So we can substitute. Then (2a) becomes:

╬▒ K - 2 y = (╬▒^2 |P|^2)/2 - 2.

(H - M)┬Ę(P - N) = 0.

Compute H - M = (p_x - m, h_H - 1). P - N = (p_x - n, p_y - 1). Dot:

(p_x - m)*(p_x - n) + (h_H - 1)*(p_y - 1) = 0.

Thus (h_H - 1)*(p_y - 1) = - (p_x - m)*(p_x - n).

Now, compute p_y - 1 = (1 + t/s)/2 - 1 = (1 + t/s - 2)/2 = (t/s - 1)/2 = (t - s)/(2s). So p_y - 1 = (t - s) / (2s). That's interesting. So p_y - 1 can be positive or negative depending on t and s.

p_x = (t - 1/s)/2.
m = (s - 1/s)/2.

p_x - m = (t - s)/2.
p_x - n = -(t - s) / (2st).

Now, compute (p_x - m)*(p_x - n) = ((t - s)/2) * ( -(t - s) / (2st) ) = - (t - s)^2 / (4 s t). So

(p_x - m)*(p_x - n) = - (t - s)^2 / (4 s t).

Now, p_y - 1 = (t - s) / (2 s). So

(p_y - 1) = (t - s) / (2 s).

Thus the fraction (p_x - m)*(p_x - n) / (p_y - 1) = [ - (t - s)^2 / (4 s t) ] / [ (t - s) / (2 s) ] = - (t - s)^2 / (4 s t) * (2 s) / (t - s) = - (t - s) / (2 t) * (1)?? Let's compute:

( - (t - s)^2 / (4 s t) ) * (2 s) / (t - s) = - (t - s)^2 * 2 s / (4 s t (t - s)) = - (t - s) * (2 s) / (4 s t) = - (t - s) / (2 t). The s cancels. So

(p_x - m)*(p_x - n) / (p_y - 1) = - (t - s) / (2 t).

Thus

Let's proceed step by step.

We have:

s > 0, t > 0.

Define:

v1 = p1 = (s t - 1) / (2 s).
v2 = p2 = (s + t) / (2 s).

|v|^2 = (s^2 t^2 + s^2 + t^2 + 1) / (4 s^2) = D / (4 s^2).

Now, ╬▒ = 2 A1 / D, where A1 = s^3 t + s t + s^2 + 1.
╬▓ = 2 (s / t) A2 / D, where A2 = s t^3 + s t + t^2 + 1.

Now, compute ╬▒ + ╬▓:

╬▒ + ╬▓ = (2/D) [ A1 + (s / t) A2 ].

Simplify inside:

A1 + (s / t) A2 = (s^3 t + s t + s^2 + 1) + (s / t) (s t^3 + s t + t^2 + 1).

Compute (s / t) * (s t^3) = s^2 t^2.
(s / t) * (s t) = s^2.
(s / t) * (t^2) = s t.
(s / t) * 1 = s / t.

So (s / t) A2 = s^2 t^2 + s^2 + s t + s / t.

Thus

A1 + (s / t) A2 = s^3 t + s t + s^2 + 1 + s^2 t^2 + s^2 + s t + s / t.

Combine like terms:

s^3 t term: s^3 t.
s t terms: s t + s t = 2 s t.
s^2 terms: s^2 + s^2 = 2 s^2.
s^2 t^2 term: s^2 t^2.
constant: 1.
s / t term: s / t.

So

A1 + (s / t) A2 = s^3 t + s^2 t^2 + 2 s t + 2 s^2 + 1 + s / t.

Now, K = ((╬▒+╬▓)/2) |v|^2 = ( (2/D) [A1 + (s/t) A2] / 2 ) * |v|^2? Actually ╬▒+╬▓ = (2/D) * (A1 + (s/t) A2). Then K = ((╬▒+╬▓)/2) * |v|^2 = ( (2/D) * (A1 + (s/t) A2) ) / 2 * |v|^2 = (1/D) * (A1 + (s/t) A2) * |v|^2. So

K = (A1 + (s/t) A2) * |v|^2 / D.

Now, |v|^2 = D / (4 s^2). So

K = (A1 + (s/t) A2) * (D / (4 s^2)) / D = (A1 + (s/t) A2) / (4 s^2). So

K = (A1 + (s/t) A2) / (4 s^2).

Now, compute A1 + (s/t) A2 as above:

S = s^3 t + s^2 t^2 + 2 s t + 2 s^2 + 1 + s / t.

Thus K = S / (4 s^2).

Now, we also have that v┬ĘO = K. So

v1 x + v2 y = K.   (1)

Now, compute y from (B) using ╬▒ and |v|^2.

We have:

y = (╬▒ K)/2 - (╬▒^2 |v|^2)/4 + 1.

We need to compute ╬▒ K and ╬▒^2 |v|^2. Let's compute ╬▒ in terms of D. ╬▒ = 2 A1 / D. So

╬▒ K = (2 A1 / D) * (S / (4 s^2)) = (2 A1 S) / (4 D s^2) = (A1 S) / (2 D s^2).

Then (╬▒ K)/2 = (A1 S) / (4 D s^2).

Next, ╬▒^2 |v|^2 = (4 A1^2 / D^2) * (D / (4 s^2)) = (4 A1^2 / D^2) * (D / (4 s^2)) = (A1^2) / (D s^2). Because 4/4 = 1, and D^2 in denominator times D gives D in denominator. So

╬▒^2 |v|^2 = A1^2 / (D s^2).

Then (╬▒^2 |v|^2)/4 = A1^2 / (4 D s^2).

Thus

y = (A1 S) / (4 D s^2) - A1^2 / (4 D s^2) + 1 = (1/(4 D s^2)) (A1 S - A1^2) + 1.

Simplify A1 S - A1^2 = A1 (S - A1). So

y = A1 (S - A1) / (4 D s^2) + 1.

Now, S - A1 = (s^3 t + s^2 t^2 + 2 s t + 2 s^2 + 1 + s / t) - (s^3 t + s t + s^2 + 1) = (s^3 t cancels, 2 s t - s t = s t, 2 s^2 - s^2 = s^2, 1 cancels, s / t remains). So

S - A1 = s t + s^2 + s / t.

Thus

y = A1 * (s t + s^2 + s / t) / (4 D s^2) + 1.

Now, A1 = s^3 t + s t + s^2 + 1. So

We can solve using Cramer's rule. Compute determinant ╬ö = p * (2 - ╬▒ q) - q * (-╬▒ p) = p (2 - ╬▒ q) + ╬▒ p q = p (2 - ╬▒ q + ╬▒ q) = 2 p. So ╬ö = 2 p. That's neat! Because:

Now t_E = -2 (A┬Ęv) / |v|^2 = -2 (x0 p + y0 q - 1) / |v|^2.

So E = A + t_E v.

Similarly, compute (A - N)┬Ęv. A - N = (x0 - d, y0). Then (A - N)┬Ęv = (x0 - d)(p - x0) + y0(q - y0) = (x0 - d)(p - x0) + y0 q - y0^2.

Simplify: (x0 - d)(p - x0) = (x0 - d)p - (x0 - d)x0 = p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0. Then plus y0 q - y0^2.

So (A - N)┬Ęv = p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0 + y0 q - y0^2.

Now x0^2 + y0^2 = 1, so -x0^2 - y0^2 = -1. Then:

(A - N)┬Ęv = p x0 - p d + d x0 + y0 q - 1.

Thus (A - N)┬Ęv = p x0 + y0 q + d x0 - p d - 1.

Now s_F = -2 ((A - N)┬Ęv) / |v|^2.

So F = A + s_F v.

(2): p_x * d + p_y * h = (d^2 + h^2)/2.

Subtract (1) from (2): p_x (d - c) = ((d^2 + h^2) - (c^2 + h^2))/2 = (d^2 - c^2)/2 = ((d - c)(d + c))/2.

Since d - c > 0 (assuming n > m, and r>0, R>0). So we can divide by (d - c):

p_x = (d + c)/2.

Thus p_x = (c + d)/2. That's interesting. So the x-coordinate of P is the midpoint of C_x and D_x. That's a nice result.

c^2 + c d + 2 p_y h = c^2 + h^2 ŌåÆ cancel c^2 ŌåÆ c d + 2 p_y h = h^2 ŌåÆ 2 p_y h = h^2 - c d.

R^2 = n^2 + h^2.  (2)

Now, C is on ╬® and on MN. Since MN is horizontal, the intersection of ╬® with line y = h: solve (x - m)^2 + (h - h)^2 = r^2 ŌåÆ (x - m)^2 = r^2 ŌåÆ x - m = ┬▒ r ŌåÆ x = m ┬▒ r. Now, P is circumcenter of A C D. Since A is origin, we have:

P┬ĘC = |C|^2 / 2,   (3)
P┬ĘD = |D|^2 / 2.   (4)

LetŌĆÖs compute C and D:

C = (c, h) with c = m - r.
D = (d, h) with d = n + R.

p_x = (c + d)/2.   (5)

Compute H - M = (p_x - m, h_H - h). P - N = (p_x - n, p_y - h). Dot:

(p_x - m)*(p_x - n) + (h_H - h)*(p_y - h) = 0.

Thus (h_H - h)*(p_y - h) = - (p_x - m)*(p_x - n). So

h_H = h - (p_x - m)*(p_x - n) / (p_y - h).   (7)

╬▒^2 |P|^2 - 2 ╬▒ (P┬ĘM) + r^2 = r^2 ŌåÆ ╬▒^2 |P|^2 - 2 ╬▒ (P┬ĘM) = 0 ŌåÆ ╬▒ (╬▒ |P|^2 - 2 P┬ĘM) = 0.

╬▒ = 0 gives A. So the other is ╬▒ = 2 (P┬ĘM) / |P|^2. So ╬▒ = 2 (P┬ĘM) / |P|^2.

Let's attempt to compute everything symbolically. I'll define:

h = 1 (without loss of generality). So A = (0,0). MN is y = 1. M = (u, 1), N = (v, 1) with v > u. Then:

r^2 = u^2 + 1.
R^2 = v^2 + 1.

C = (u - r, 1).
D = (v + R, 1).

Now, we can compute P:

p_x = (c + d)/2 = ( (u - r) + (v + R) ) / 2 = (u + v + (R - r))/2.

p_y = (1 - c d) / (2*1) = (1 - (u - r)*(v + R)) / 2.

So P = (p_x, p_y). That's fine.

Now, compute H:

H = (p_x, h_H) with h_H = 1 - (p_x - u)*(p_x - v) / (p_y - 1). Since p_y - 1 = p_y - 1.

(s + t) / (2 s) = (2 s (s + t)) / (4 s^2) = (2 s (s + t)) / (4 s^2). So

P┬ĘM = [ (s t - 1)*(s^2 - 1) + 2 s (s + t) ] / (4 s^2).   (1)

Similarly, P┬ĘN = p1 * n + p2.

n = (t^2 - 1) / (2 t). So p1 * n = ((s t - 1) / (2 s)) * ((t^2 - 1) / (2 t)) = ( (s t - 1)*(t^2 - 1) ) / (4 s t). Then p2 = (s + t) / (2 s). So

(s + t) / (2 s) = (2 t (s + t)) / (4 s t). So

P┬ĘN = [ (s t - 1)*(t^2 - 1) + 2 t (s + t) ] / (4 s t).   (2)

S = a^3 b + a^2 b^2 + 2 a b + 2 a^2 + 1 + a / b

We have ╬▒ = 2 A1 / D
K = S / (4 a^2)

We have hy = (3b - a) / (2b)

Now, we need to compute O = (x,y) from the linear system. We have:

y = (R2 + ╬▒ K) / 2, with R2 = 2 - A1^2 / (2 D a^2). That's okay.

But we also have from Cramer's rule:

x = ( K (2 - ╬▒ q) - q R2 ) / (2 p)

We can compute these and then compute det(O - H, v). However maybe we can avoid computing x explicitly by using the fact that O is the circumcenter, so we could also compute O - H using the expression for H and maybe relate to something like (B - E) or (B - F). But let's compute.

First, compute ╬▒ q = (2 A1 / D) * ((a + b) / (2a)) = A1 (a + b) / (a D). So

2 - ╬▒ q = 2 - A1 (a + b) / (a D).

Similarly, ╬▒ p = A1 (ab - 1) / (a D). That's something.

Now, R2 = 2 - A1^2 / (2 D a^2). So

╬▒ K = (2 A1 / D) * (S / (4 a^2)) = (A1 S) / (2 D a^2). Then

y = (R2 + ╬▒ K) / 2 = (2 - A1^2 / (2 D a^2) + A1 S / (2 D a^2)) / 2 = 1 - A1^2 / (4 D a^2) + A1 S / (4 D a^2) = 1 + (A1 S - A1^2) / (4 D a^2). That's our expression. So

y = 1 + (A1 (S - A1)) / (4 D a^2). And S - A1 = a b + a^2 + a / b. So

y = 1 + (A1 (a b + a^2 + a / b)) / (4 D a^2) = 1 + (A1 (a b + a^2 + a / b)) / (4 D a^2). Simplify (a b + a^2 + a / b) = a (b + a + 1 / b). So

y = 1 + (A1 * a (b + a + 1 / b)) / (4 D a^2) = 1 + (A1 (b + a + 1 / b)) / (4 D a). So

y = 1 + (A1 (a + b + 1 / b)) / (4 D a). That's a nicer expression. Good.

Now, we also need x. Let's compute x using the formula x = (K (2 - ╬▒ q) - q R2) / (2 p). Since p might be zero, we'll treat that case separately. For now, assume ab ŌēĀ 1.

Compute K = S / (4 a^2). So K (2 - ╬▒ q) = (S / (4 a^2)) * (2 - ╬▒ q). Then q R2 = q * (2 - A1^2 / (2 D a^2)). So

x = ( (S / (4 a^2)) * (2 - ╬▒ q) - q * (2 - A1^2 / (2 D a^2)) ) ) / (2 p).

Simplify. But note that we also have an expression for y. Perhaps we can compute O - H and then det.

But maybe there is a smarter approach: Instead of solving for O, we can compute the power of H with respect to (BEF) and then show that the square of the distance from H to the line L equals that power, which would imply that L is tangent? Not exactly. Actually if a line L passes through H and is tangent to the circle, then the length of the tangent from H to the circle is the distance from H to the point of tangency, which is sqrt(power). But if H lies on the tangent line, then the tangent from H to the circle is not along that line unless H is the point of tangency. So that's not.

But we can consider the following: For a given circle, if a point X lies on the circle, then the tangent at X is the line perpendicular to OX. So if we can find a point X on (BEF) such that OX is parallel to something, and then show that the line through H parallel to AP is that tangent, then we need to prove that H lies on that tangent line. ## Solution
We present a detailed analytic solution. We set up a convenient coordinate system and use algebraic manipulation to prove the required tangency.

### 1.  Preliminary coordinate choices

Place the point \(A\) at the origin and rotate the plane so that the line \(AP\) becomes the \(x\)-axis.  (We will later see that \(AP\) is indeed a line through \(A\); the problem defines \(P\) as the circumcenter of \(\triangle ACD\) and then the line \(AP\) is drawn, so we may rotate to make it horizontal.)  Let the line \(MN\) (the line of centers) be horizontal at height \(h\neq0\) (since the circles intersect in two points, the line of centers does not pass through \(A\); thus \(h\neq0\) and we may scale so that \(h=1\) after a similarity transformation).  Because similarity transformations preserve circles, tangency and the orthocenters, we can assume without loss of generality that

\[
A=(0,0),\qquad MN\ \text{is the line}\ y=1.
\]

Let the centres be

\[
M=(m,1),\qquad N=(n,1)
\]

with \(n>m\) (so that the order \(C,M,N,D\) along \(MN\) is as given).  Since \(A\) lies on both circles,

\[
|M|=r,\qquad |N|=R,
\]

where \(r\) and \(R\) are the radii of \(\Omega\) and \(\Gamma\) respectively.  Therefore

\[
m^{2}+1=r^{2},\qquad n^{2}+1=R^{2}. \tag{1}
\]

The line \(MN\) (the line \(y=1\)) intersects \(\Omega\) at two points; the one that is named \(C\) lies to the left of \(M\) (because \(C,M,N\) are collinear in that order), hence

\[
C=(m-r,1).
\]

Similarly, the intersection of \(\Gamma\) with the line \(y=1\) that is to the right of \(N\) is

\[
D=(n+R,1).
\]

### 2.  A convenient parametrisation that eliminates square roots

Introduce positive parameters \(s\) and \(t\) by

\[
s = m+r,\qquad t = n+R.
\]

From (1) we have

\[
m = \frac{s-\frac1s}{2},\qquad r = \frac{s+\frac1s}{2},\qquad
n = \frac{t-\frac1t}{2},\qquad R = \frac{t+\frac1t}{2}.
\]

Indeed, because \((m+r)(m-r)=m^{2}-r^{2}=-1\) and similarly for \(n,R\).  Consequently

\[
C = (m-r,1)=\Bigl(-\frac1s,\,1\Bigr),\qquad
D = (n+R,1)=\bigl(t,\,1\bigr).
\]

The circumcenter \(P\) of \(\triangle ACD\) satisfies \(|P|=|P-C|=|P-D|\).  Because \(A\) is the origin, the conditions become

\[
P\cdot C = \frac{|C|^{2}}{2},\qquad P\cdot D = \frac{|D|^{2}}{2}. \tag{2}
\]

Let \(P=(p_{1},p_{2})\).  Substituting \(C\) and \(D\),

\[
p_{1}\Bigl(-\frac1s\Bigr)+p_{2}\cdot1 = \frac{(-1/s)^{2}+1^{2}}{2}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad -\frac{p_{1}}{s}+p_{2}= \frac{1+\frac1{s^{2}}}{2},
\]
\[
p_{1}\,t+p_{2}\cdot1 = \frac{t^{2}+1^{2}}{2}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad p_{1}\,t+p_{2}= \frac{t^{2}+1}{2}.
\]

Solving these two linear equations for \(p_{1},p_{2}\) yields

\[
p_{1}= \frac{t-\frac1s}{2},\qquad
p_{2}= \frac{1+\frac{t}{s}}{2}. \tag{3}
\]

Thus

\[
P = \Bigl(\frac{t-\frac1s}{2},\; \frac{1+\frac{t}{s}}{2}\Bigr).
\]

### 3.  The orthocentre \(H\) of \(\triangle PMN\)

The triangle \(PMN\) has vertices

\[
P=(p_{1},p_{2}),\qquad M=(m,1)=\Bigl(\frac{s-\frac1s}{2},\,1\Bigr),\qquad
N=(n,1)=\Bigl(\frac{t-\frac1t}{2},\,1\Bigr).
\]

Since \(MN\) is horizontal, the altitude from \(P\) is vertical; therefore the orthocentre \(H\) has the same \(x\)-coordinate as \(P\):

\[
H = \bigl(p_{1},\,h_{y}\bigr).
\]

The altitude from \(M\) is perpendicular to \(PN\).  Using the dotŌĆæproduct condition \((H-M)\cdot(P-N)=0\),

\[
(p_{1}-m,\; h_{y}-1)\cdot(p_{1}-n,\; p_{2}-1)=0.
\]

Plug in the expressions for \(m,n,p_{1},p_{2}\) (which are rational in \(s,t\)).  A direct computation gives

\[
p_{1}-m = \frac{t-s}{2},\qquad
p_{1}-n = \frac{\frac1t-\frac1s}{2}= \frac{s-t}{2st},\qquad
p_{2}-1 = \frac{t-s}{2s}.
\]

Hence

\[
(p_{1}-m)(p_{1}-n)+(h_{y}-1)(p_{2}-1)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Bigl(\frac{t-s}{2}\Bigr)\Bigl(\frac{s-t}{2st}\Bigr)+(h_{y}-1)\Bigl(\frac{t-s}{2s}\Bigr)=0.
\]

Simplify the first term: \(\frac{t-s}{2}\cdot\frac{s-t}{2st}= -\frac{(t-s)^{2}}{4st}\).  The equation becomes

\[
-\frac{(t-s)^{2}}{4st} + (h_{y}-1)\frac{t-s}{2s}=0.
\]

If \(t=s\) then the circles are tangent (they would intersect in one point), contradicting the hypothesis of two distinct intersections.  Thus \(t\neq s\) and we may cancel \(\frac{t-s}{2s}\) (nonŌĆæzero) to obtain

\[
-\frac{t-s}{2t} + (h_{y}-1)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
h_{y}=1+\frac{t-s}{2t}= \frac{3t-s}{2t}. \tag{4}
\]

Therefore

\[
H = \Bigl(\frac{t-\frac1s}{2},\; \frac{3t-s}{2t}\Bigr). \tag{5}
\]

### 4.  The points \(E\) and \(F\)

The line \(AP\) passes through the origin and \(P\); hence its parametric form is \( \lambda P\).  The second intersections of this line with the circles are

\[
E = \alpha P,\qquad F = \beta P,
\]

where the scalars \(\alpha,\beta\) are determined by the equations \(| \alpha P - M |^{2}=r^{2}\) and \(| \beta P - N |^{2}=R^{2}\) (the circles pass through \(A\)).

For \(\Omega\):  \(| \alpha P - M|^{2}=r^{2}\) and \(|M|^{2}=r^{2}\) give

\[
\alpha^{2}|P|^{2} - 2\alpha\,(P\cdot M) = 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\alpha = \frac{2\,(P\cdot M)}{|P|^{2}}.
\]

Similarly

\[
\beta = \frac{2\,(P\cdot N)}{|P|^{2}}. \tag{6}
\]

We now compute these expressions in terms of \(s,t\).  From (3),

\[
P = \Bigl(\frac{st-1}{2s},\; \frac{s+t}{2s}\Bigr). \tag{7}
\]

Then

\[
P\cdot M = \frac{st-1}{2s}\cdot\frac{s-\frac1s}{2} + \frac{s+t}{2s}\cdot1
= \frac{(st-1)(s^{2}-1)}{4s^{2}} + \frac{s+t}{2s}.
\]

Simplify the numerator:

\[
(st-1)(s^{2}-1) = s^{3}t - s t - s^{2} + 1.
\]

Hence

\[
P\cdot M = \frac{s^{3}t - s t - s^{2}+1}{4s^{2}} + \frac{s+t}{2s}
= \frac{s^{3}t - s t - s^{2}+1 + 2s(s+t)}{4s^{2}}.
\]

But \(2s(s+t) = 2s^{2}+2st\).  Therefore

\[
P\cdot M = \frac{s^{3}t - s t - s^{2}+1 + 2s^{2}+2st}{4s^{2}}
= \frac{s^{3}t + s t + s^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}. \tag{8}
\]

Similarly,

\[
P\cdot N = \frac{st-1}{2s}\cdot\frac{t-\frac1t}{2} + \frac{s+t}{2s}\cdot1
= \frac{(st-1)(t^{2}-1)}{4s t} + \frac{s+t}{2s}.
\]

Compute \((st-1)(t^{2}-1) = s t^{3} - s t - t^{2} + 1\).  Then

\[
P\cdot N = \frac{s t^{3} - s t - t^{2}+1}{4s t} + \frac{s+t}{2s}
= \frac{s t^{3} - s t - t^{2}+1 + 2t(s+t)}{4s t}.
\]

Now \(2t(s+t) = 2st + 2t^{2}\).  So

\[
P\cdot N = \frac{s t^{3} - s t - t^{2}+1 + 2st + 2t^{2}}{4s t}
= \frac{s t^{3} + s t + t^{2}+1}{4s t}. \tag{9}
\]

Next compute \(|P|^{2}\).  From (7),

\[
|P|^{2}= \frac{(st-1)^{2}}{4s^{2}} + \frac{(s+t)^{2}}{4s^{2}}
= \frac{(st-1)^{2}+(s+t)^{2}}{4s^{2}}.
\]

Expand:

\[
(st-1)^{2}+(s+t)^{2}= s^{2}t^{2}-2st+1 + s^{2}+2st+t^{2}= s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1.
\]

Thus

\[
|P|^{2}= \frac{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}. \tag{10}
\]

Now using (6) and (8),(9),(10),

\[
\alpha = \frac{2\,(P\cdot M)}{|P|^{2}}
= \frac{2\cdot \frac{s^{3}t+st+s^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}}{\frac{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}}
= \frac{2\,(s^{3}t+st+s^{2}+1)}{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}. \tag{11}
\]

\[
\beta = \frac{2\,(P\cdot N)}{|P|^{2}}
= \frac{2\cdot \frac{s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1}{4s t}}{\frac{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}}
= \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)\,s}{s t\,(s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1)}? Wait, compute carefully:

\[
\beta = \frac{2\,(P\cdot N)}{|P|^{2}} = \frac{2\cdot \frac{s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1}{4s t}}{\frac{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}}
= \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)}{4s t}\cdot\frac{4s^{2}}{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}
= \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)\,s}{s t\,(s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1)}? Actually:

\[
\frac{2\cdot \frac{s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1}{4s t}}{\frac{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}}
= \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)}{4s t}} \cdot \frac{4s^{2}}{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}
= \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)\,s}{s t\,(s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1)}? Let's do step by step:

\[
\frac{2\,(P\cdot N)}{|P|^{2}} = \frac{2\cdot \frac{s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1}{4s t}}{\frac{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}{4s^{2}}}
= \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)}{4s t} \cdot \frac{4s^{2}}{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}
= \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)\,s^{2}}{s t\,(s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1)}.
\]

But note that \(s^{2} / (s t) = s / t\). So

\[
\beta = \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)\,s}{t\,(s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1)}. \tag{12}
\]

### 5.  The circumcircle of \(\triangle BEF\)

The other intersection point \(B\) of the circles \(\Omega\) and \(\Gamma\) is the reflection of \(A\) across the line \(y=1\).  Since \(A=(0,0)\) and the line \(y=1\) is horizontal, we obtain

\[
B = (0,2). \tag{13}
\]

The points \(E\) and \(F\) lie on the line \(AP\) (through the origin with direction \(P\)).  Write \(v = P\) for brevity.  Then

\[
E = \alpha v,\qquad F = \beta v.
\]

Let \(O\) be the circumcenter of \(\triangle BEF\).  Because \(E\) and \(F\) are collinear with the origin, the perpendicular bisector of \(EF\) is the line orthogonal to \(v\) through the midpoint of \(EF\).  That gives

\[
O\cdot v = \frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\,|v|^{2}. \tag{14}
\]

The perpendicular bisector of \(BE\) gives

\[
O\cdot (B-E) = \frac{|B|^{2}-|E|^{2}}{2}. \tag{15}
\]

Substituting \(B=(0,2)\) and \(E=\alpha v\),

\[
O\cdot (-\alpha v + (0,2)) = \frac{4-\alpha^{2}|v|^{2}}{2}.
\]

Hence

\[
-\alpha\,(O\cdot v) + 2\,(O\cdot (0,1)) = 2 - \frac{\alpha^{2}|v|^{2}}{2}.
\]

But \(O\cdot (0,1) = y\) (the \(y\)-coordinate of \(O\)).  Thus

\[
-\alpha\,(O\cdot v) + 2y = 2 - \frac{\alpha^{2}|v|^{2}}{2}. \tag{16}
\]

Similarly, using \(F\) we would obtain an analogous equation; they are consistent because (14) holds.

Now we have two linear equations in the coordinates of \(O\).  Write \(O=(x,y)\).  Equation (14) becomes

\[
p\,x + q\,y = K,\qquad\text{where}\quad K=\frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\,|v|^{2}. \tag{17}
\]

Equation (16) becomes

\[
-\alpha\,(p\,x+q\,y) + 2y = 2 - \frac{\alpha^{2}|v|^{2}}{2}.
\]

But \(p\,x+q\,y = K\) from (17), so

\[
-\alpha K + 2y = 2 - \frac{\alpha^{2}|v|^{2}}{2}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
2y = 2 - \frac{\alpha^{2}|v|^{2}}{2} + \alpha K.
\]

Therefore

\[
y = 1 - \frac{\alpha^{2}|v|^{2}}{4} + \frac{\alpha K}{2}. \tag{18}
\]

Now we need to compute \(K\) and \(\alpha\) in terms of \(s,t\) and then simplify the expression for \(y\) and also find \(x\) (though we may not need \(x\) explicitly).  However, it turns out that the distance from \(O\) to the line \(L\) (through \(H\) parallel to \(v\)) equals the radius of \((BEF)\), which can be checked using the coordinates we obtain.

From (17) and the expression for \(y\) we can also solve for \(x\) using Cramer's rule, but we will later see that the determinant condition simplifies nicely.  Let's compute the needed quantities.

First, compute \(|v|^{2}\) and \(\alpha\) in terms of \(s,t\).  From (10),

\[
|v|^{2}= \frac{s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1}{4s^{2}} = \frac{D}{4s^{2}},
\]

where \(D = s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+t^{2}+1\).

From (11),

\[
\alpha = \frac{2\,(s^{3}t+st+s^{2}+1)}{D}.
\]

Now compute \(K = \frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\,|v|^{2}\).  But we can also compute \(K\) directly from the formula for the perpendicular bisector of \(EF\): \(K = \frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}|v|^{2}\).  Using (11) and (12) we can find \(\alpha+\beta\) as a rational expression.

Compute \(\alpha+\beta\):

\[
\alpha+\beta = \frac{2\,(s^{3}t+st+s^{2}+1)}{D} + \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)\,s}{t\,D}?
\]

Wait, we had \(\beta\) in (12): \(\beta = \frac{2\,(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1)\,s}{t\,D}\).  So

\[
\alpha+\beta = \frac{2}{D}\Bigl( s^{3}t+st+s^{2}+1 + \frac{s}{t}(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1) \Bigr).
\]

Simplify the second term:

\[
\frac{s}{t}(s t^{3}+st+t^{2}+1) = s^{2} t^{2} + s^{2} + \frac{s t}{t}? Actually:
\frac{s}{t} \cdot s t^{3} = s^{2} t^{2},
\frac{s}{t} \cdot s t = s^{2},
\frac{s}{t} \cdot t^{2} = s t,
\frac{s}{t} \cdot 1 = \frac{s}{t}.
\]

Thus

\[
\alpha+\beta = \frac{2}{D}\Bigl( s^{3}t+st+s^{2}+1 + s^{2}t^{2}+s^{2}+s t+\frac{s}{t} \Bigr).
\]

Combine like terms:

\[
s^{3}t \text{ (unchanged)},\quad
s t \text{ from first term} + s t \text{ from second} = 2 s t,\quad
s^{2} \text{ from first} + s^{2} \text{ from second} = 2 s^{2},\quad
s^{2}t^{2} \text{ from second},\quad
1 \text{ from first},\quad
\frac{s}{t} \text{ from second}.
\]

So

\[
\alpha+\beta = \frac{2}{D}\bigl( s^{3}t + s^{2}t^{2} + 2 s t + 2 s^{2} + 1 + \frac{s}{t} \bigr). \tag{19}
\]

Now \(K = \frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\,|v|^{2} = \frac{\alpha+\beta}{2} \cdot \frac{D}{4 s^{2}} = \frac{\alpha+\beta}{8 s^{2}} \cdot D\).  Substitute (19):

\[
K = \frac{2}{D}\bigl( s^{3}t + s^{2}t^{2} + 2 s t + 2 s^{2} + 1 + \frac{s}{t} \bigr) \cdot \frac{D}{8 s^{2}} = \frac{2}{8 s^{2}}\bigl( s^{3}t + s^{2}t^{2} + 2 s t + 2 s^{2} + 1 + \frac{s}{t} \bigr) = \frac{1}{4 s^{2}}\bigl( s^{3}t + s^{2}t^{2} + 2 s t + 2 s^{2} + 1 + \frac{s}{t} \bigr). \tag{
